The winner is the first player to form an unbroken chain of five stones horizontally, vertically, or diagonally.\r\nIt originated in Japan during the Heian period[citation needed]. The name \"Gomoku\" is from the Japanese language, in which it is referred to as gomokunarabe (‰∫îÁõÆ‰∏¶„Åπ). Go means five, moku is a counter word for pieces and narabe means line-up. The game is also popular in Korea, where it is called omok (Ïò§Î™© [‰∫îÁõÆ]) which has the same structure and origin as the Japanese name.\r\nThe Japanese call this game Go-moku (five stones).
